CC   -!- FUNCTION: The A chain is responsible for inhibiting protein
CC       synthesis through the catalytic inactivation of 60S ribosomal
CC       subunits by removing adenine from position 4,324 of 28S rRNA. The
CC       B chain binds to cell receptors and probably facilitates the entry
CC       into the cell of the A chain; B chains are also responsible for
CC       cell agglutination (lectin activity). Inhibits growth of the human
CC       tumor cell line Molt4. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:1450445,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15001393, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15182350}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of the N-glycosidic bond at one
CC       specific adenosine on the 28S rRNA.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Disulfide-linked dimer of A and B chains.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12351890, ECO:0000269|PubMed:12823544,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:16508080}.
CC   -!- PTM: The A chain of variant MLA' is not glycosylated.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12823544}.
CC   -!- PHARMACEUTICAL: Due to its immunomodulative effects it is being
CC       studied in clinical trials in cancer patients as it may slow the
CC       growth of cancer cells and be an effective treatment for solid
CC       tumors.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Several isoforms exist.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the ribosome-inactivating protein family.
CC       Type 2 RIP subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Ricin is highly toxic to animal cells and to a lesser
CC       extent to plant cells. The A chain acts as a glycosidase that
CC       removes a specific adenine residue from an exposed loop of the 28S
CC       rRNA (A4324 in mammals), leading to rRNA breakage. As this loop is
CC       involved in elongation factor binding, modified ribosomes are
CC       catalytically inactive and unable to support protein synthesis.
CC       The A chain can inactivate a few thousand ribosomes per minute,
CC       faster than the cell can make new ones. Therefore a single A chain
CC       molecule can kill an animal cell. The B chain binds to beta-D-
CC       galactopyranoside moieties on cell surface glycoproteins and
CC       glycolipids and facilitates the entry into the cell of the A
CC       chain; B chains are also responsible for cell agglutination
CC       (Lectin activity).
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of the N-glycosidic bond at one
CC       specific adenosine on the 28S rRNA.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Disulfide-linked dimer of A and B chains.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The B chain is composed of two domains, each domain
CC       consists of 3 homologous subdomains (alpha, beta, gamma).
CC   -!- BIOTECHNOLOGY: A deglycosylated A chain may be linked to
CC       monoclonal antibodies to produce immunotoxins exploited in cancer
CC       treatment. However, a point mutation should be introduced to
CC       eliminate vascular leak syndrome, a side effect resulting from
CC       endothelial damage.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: In the N-terminal section; belongs to the ribosome-
CC       inactivating protein family. Type 2 RIP subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: The A chain is responsible for inhibiting protein
CC       synthesis through the catalytic inactivation of 60S ribosomal
CC       subunits by removing adenine from position 4,324 of 28S rRNA. The
CC       B chain binds to cell receptors and probably facilitates the entry
CC       into the cell of the A chain; B chains are also responsible for
CC       cell agglutination (lectin activity). Inhibits growth of the human
CC       tumor cell line Molt4. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:1450445,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15001393, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15182350}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of the N-glycosidic bond at one
CC       specific adenosine on the 28S rRNA.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Disulfide-linked dimer of A and B chains.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=59300; Method=MALDI; Range=34-569;
CC       Evidence={ECO:0000269|PubMed:15635663};
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Several isoforms exist.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the ribosome-inactivating protein family.

CC       synthesis through the catalytic inactivation of 60S ribosomal
CC       subunits by removing adenine from position 4,324 of 28S rRNA (By
CC       similarity). Less toxic than abrin-a.

CC       endocytosis. {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P28590}.

CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16772301}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The B chain is composed of two domains, each domain
CC       consists of 3 homologous subdomains (alpha, beta, gamma).
CC       {ECO:0000255}.

CC       splenocytes and thymocytes in mice. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15474989}.

CC       inactivating protein family. Type 2 RIP subfamily. {ECO:0000255}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: The A chain is responsible for inhibiting protein
CC       synthesis through the catalytic inactivation of 60S ribosomal
CC       subunits by removing adenine from position 4,324 of 28S rRNA.
CC       Abrin-a is more toxic than ricin.
CC   -!- FUNCTION: The B chain is a galactose-specific lectin that
CC       facilitates the binding of abrin to the cell membrane that
CC       precedes endocytosis.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of the N-glycosidic bond at one
CC       specific adenosine on the 28S rRNA.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Disulfide-linked dimer of A and B chains.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The B chain is composed of two domains, each domain
CC       consists of 3 homologous subdomains (alpha, beta, gamma).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: In the N-terminal section; belongs to the ribosome-
CC       inactivating protein family. Type 2 RIP subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Neu5Ac(alpha2-6)Gal/GalNAc specific agglutinin
CC       (PubMed:3805045). Behaves as a type-2 ribosome-inactivating
CC       protein (PubMed:8631319). Strongly inhibits mammalian but not
CC       plant ribosomes (PubMed:8631319). The A chain is responsible for
CC       inhibiting protein synthesis through the catalytic inactivation of
CC       60S ribosomal subunits by removing adenine from position 4,324 of
CC       28S rRNA (Probable). The B chain binds to cell receptors and
CC       probably facilitates the entry into the cell of the A chain; B
CC       chains are also responsible for cell agglutination (lectin
CC       activity) (Probable). Involved in plant defense against insects
CC       (By similarity). {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:O22415,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:3805045, ECO:0000269|PubMed:8631319,
CC       ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- FUNCTION: TrSNAI: Binds Neu5Ac(alpha2-6)Gal/GalNAc but has no
CC       clear agglutination activity. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:9541002}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of the N-glycosidic bond at one
CC       specific adenosine on the 28S rRNA.
CC       {ECO:0000255|RuleBase:RU004915}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Tetramer of four pairs of disulfide bound A-B chains.
CC       {ECO:0000305|PubMed:8631319}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in bark.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8631319}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The B-chain consists of six tandemly repeated subdomains.
CC       Only subdomains 1-alpha and 2-gamma possess a functional
CC       carbohydrate-binding site. {ECO:0000305|PubMed:8631319}.
CC   -!- PTM: The precursor is processed in two chains, A and B, that are
CC       linked by a disulfide bond (PubMed:9541002). A small truncated
CC       form corresponding roughly to the second ricin B-type lectin
CC       domain of the B chain, TrSNAI, can also be produced
CC       (PubMed:9541002). {ECO:0000269|PubMed:9541002}.
CC   -!- PTM: Glycosylated (PubMed:8631319, PubMed:27384337). N-glycans of
CC       subunit A are (Man)2-3(Xyl)(GlcNAc)2(Fuc) at Asn-40, (GlcNAc)0-
CC       2(Man)3(Xyl)(GlcNAc)2(Fuc) or (Man)1-2(GlcNAc)2 at Asn-62,
CC       (Man)3(Xyl)(GlcNAc)2(Fuc)0-1 at Asn-144 and (GlcNAc)0-
CC       1(Man)3(Xyl)(GlcNAc)2(Fuc) at Asn-260 (PubMed:27384337). N-glycans
CC       of subunit B are (Man)3(Xyl)(GlcNAc)2(Fuc) at Asn-492 and (Man)6-
CC       9(GlcNAc)2 at Asn-526 (PubMed:27384337).
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:27384337, ECO:0000269|PubMed:8631319}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the ribosome-inactivating protein family.
CC       Type 2 RIP subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.

RA   Van Damme E.J., Hao Q., Charels D., Barre A., Rouge P., Van Leuven F.,

RT   "Characterization and molecular cloning of two different type 2

RT   Polygonatum multiflorum.";

CC   -!- FUNCTION: GalNAc-specific agglutinin. Behaves as a type-2
CC       ribosome-inactivating protein. Inhibits mammalian ribosomes
CC       (PubMed:10785398). The A chain is responsible for inhibiting
CC       protein synthesis through the catalytic inactivation of 60S
CC       ribosomal subunits by removing adenine from position 4,324 of 28S
CC       rRNA (Probable). The B chain binds to cell receptors and probably
CC       facilitates the entry into the cell of the A chain; B chains are
CC       also responsible for cell agglutination (lectin activity)
CC       (Probable). Involved in plant defense against insects (By
CC       similarity). Has very low cytotoxic activity against the human
CC       tumor cell lines CEM and Molt4 (PubMed:10785398).
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:O22415, ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398,
CC       ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of the N-glycosidic bond at one
CC       specific adenosine on the 28S rRNA.
CC       {ECO:0000255|RuleBase:RU004915, ECO:0000255|SAAS:SAAS00357228,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398}.
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Strongly inhibited by asialofetuin and
CC       asialomucin. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Tetramer of four pairs of disulfide bound A-B chains.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in rhizome and more abundantly in
CC       leaves (at protein level). {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The B-chain consists of six tandemly repeated subdomains.
CC       Only subdomains 1-alpha and 2-gamma possess a functional
CC       carbohydrate-binding site. {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q41358}.
CC   -!- PTM: The precursor is processed in two chains, A and B, that are
CC       linked by a disulfide bond. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398}.
CC   -!- PTM: Glycosylated. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the ribosome-inactivating protein family.
CC       Type 2 RIP subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.

CC       tumor cell line Molt4, but higher against CEM (PubMed:10785398).
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:O22415, ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398,
CC       ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of the N-glycosidic bond at one
CC       specific adenosine on the 28S rRNA.
CC       {ECO:0000255|RuleBase:RU004915, ECO:0000255|SAAS:SAAS00357228,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398}.
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Strongly inhibited by asialofetuin and
CC       asialomucin. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Disulfide-linked dimer of A and B chains.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in rhizome and abundantly in leaves
CC       (at protein level). {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The B-chain consists of six tandemly repeated subdomains.
CC       Only subdomains 1-alpha and 2-gamma possess a functional
CC       carbohydrate-binding site. {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q41358}.
CC   -!- PTM: The precursor is processed in two chains, A and B, that are
CC       linked by a disulfide bond. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398}.
CC   -!- PTM: Glycosylated. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398}.
CC   -!- PTM: The N-terminus is blocked. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10785398}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the ribosome-inactivating protein family.
CC       Type 2 RIP subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Seed lectin similar to type 2 ribosome-inactivating
CC       proteins (PubMed:23897472, PubMed:11375527). The Aalpha and Abeta
CC       chains constitute the rRNA glycosidase domain and the B chain the
CC       carbohydrate-binding lectin domain (PubMed:23897472). Is predicted
CC       to have no glycosidase activity and, hence, to be non-toxic, due
CC       to small changes in both the nucleotide binding and carbohydrate
CC       binding capabilities (PubMed:23897472, PubMed:11375527). Binds
CC       galactose and derivatives with a preference for the beta-anomeric
CC       forms (PubMed:8799450, PubMed:10877067). Binds prophyrins
CC       (PubMed:10877067). Has hemagglutinating activity towards rabbit
CC       and human erythrocytes (PubMed:8799450, PubMed:10877067).
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10877067, ECO:0000269|PubMed:11375527,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:23897472, ECO:0000269|PubMed:8799450}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Heterotrimer consisting of Aalpha, Abeta and B chains
CC       with Abeta and B being disulfide-linked.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The B chain is composed of two domains with each domain
CC       consisting of 3 homologous subdomains (alpha, beta, gamma).
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P02879}.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=59028.6; Method=Electrospray; Range=1-519;
CC       Evidence={ECO:0000269|PubMed:23897472};
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: In the N-terminal section; belongs to the ribosome-
CC       inactivating protein family. Type 2 RIP subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- CAUTION: Was originally thought to be a heterodimer. However,
CC       methods used then would have missed the Aalpha chain.
CC       {ECO:0000305|PubMed:8799450}.
CC   -!- CAUTION: Based on similarity to other family members, it is
CC       assumed that all three chains derive from a single precursor but
CC       the genomic DNA sequence to support this is not yet available.
CC       {ECO:0000305|PubMed:23897472}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Protects the structural integrity of the neurotoxin; may
CC       increase internalization of the neurotoxin into the bloodstream of
CC       the host. Involved in binding to the small intestine through
CC       interactions with glycolipids and glycoproteins containing sialic
CC       acid moieties. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:9421908}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Botulinum toxins are produced as progenitor toxins of
CC       large molecular sizes of 12S (M toxin), 16S (L toxin) and 19S (LL
CC       toxin). M toxin consists of a nontoxic, non-hemagglutinin
CC       component (NTNHA) and the neurotoxin. L toxin consists of the M
CC       toxin and the 3 subcomponents of hemagglutinin (HA). HA is
CC       composed of subcomponents having 70, 33, and 17 kDa. The 70 kDa
CC       subcomponent undergoes proteolytic processing and is split into
CC       HA-55 and HA-22-23.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: The A chain is responsible for inhibiting protein
CC       synthesis through the catalytic inactivation of 60S ribosomal
CC       subunits by removing adenine from position 4,324 of 28S rRNA. The
CC       B chain binds to cell receptors and probably facilitates the entry
CC       into the cell of the A chain; B chains are also responsible for
CC       cell agglutination (lectin activity). Inhibits growth of the human
CC       tumor cell line Molt4. {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P81446,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:1450445, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15001393}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of the N-glycosidic bond at one
CC       specific adenosine on the 28S rRNA.
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P81446}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Disulfide-linked dimer of A and B chains.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10198229, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15583377}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Several isoforms exist.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15001393}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the ribosome-inactivating protein family.
CC       Type 2 RIP subfamily. {ECO:0000255}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Non-toxic type 2 RIP which strongly inhibits mammalian

CC       B chain binds to cell receptors and probably facilitates the entry
CC       into the cell of the A chain; B chains are also responsible for
CC       cell agglutination (lectin activity). Agglutination is inhibited
CC       by Neu5Ac(alpha2,6)lactose, and N-linked glycoproteins such as
CC       fetuin and orosomucoid. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:9183001}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of the N-glycosidic bond at one
CC       specific adenosine on the 28S rRNA.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Disulfide-linked dimer of A and B chains.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:9183001}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The B chain is composed of two domains, each domain
CC       consists of 3 homologous subdomains (alpha, beta, gamma).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: In the N-terminal section; belongs to the ribosome-
CC       inactivating protein family. Type 2 RIP subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: The A chain is responsible for inhibiting protein
CC       synthesis through the catalytic inactivation of 60S ribosomal
CC       subunits by removing adenine from position 4,324 of 28S rRNA.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- FUNCTION: The B chain is a galactose-specific lectin that
CC       facilitates the binding of abrin to the cell membrane that
CC       precedes endocytosis. {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of the N-glycosidic bond at one
CC       specific adenosine on the 28S rRNA.
CC       {ECO:0000255|RuleBase:RU003711}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Disulfide-linked dimer of A and B chains. {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The B chain is composed of two domains, each domain
CC       consists of 3 homologous subdomains (alpha, beta, gamma).
CC       {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: In the N-terminal section; belongs to the ribosome-
CC       inactivating protein family. Type 2 RIP subfamily. {ECO:0000255}.
